Current Commentary

The Enemy Crosses the Luan River, Tianjin and Beijing Are in Danger

— In Reality

Japan's invasion of our Northeast initially relied on economic weapons, focusing on market development and expanding the control of financial capital. In recent years, as the global economic panic has worsened and various countries have implemented protectionism, striving for so-called self-sufficiency, Japanese imperialists, under the guise of self-defense, have recklessly undermined our country's independence and used "anti-communism" as a pretext to confuse the great powers and gain international sympathy. If our country had fought resolutely during the September 18th Incident, even if we had failed, it would have been nothing more than international mediation, offering the five railways in the Northeast as a sacrifice. At most, Japan would have monopolized the transportation business in the Northeast and lost some economic power. The losses from defeat could still be remedied. Alternatively, we could have taken the path of direct negotiation, and the losses would have been no more than that. However, our country procrastinated between peace and war, mistakenly believing that the League of Nations had the power to restrain Japan. By the time the enemy became strong, not only had the Northeast fallen, but Rehe had also been ravaged. Japan's so-called continental policy is the last trick of the militarists to save the economic panic. Little did they know that the more military actions expanded, the more difficult the finances became, and the more profound the economic panic became. Thus, the military aggression became more and more endless. Therefore, when they attacked Shenyang, their purpose was only to gain economic rights in the Northeast. After Liaoning and Jilin were in Japanese hands, Heilongjiang, Jinzhou, and Shanhaiguan fell one after another. Rehe, with an area of 580,000 square miles, was completely occupied by the enemy. Although our voices of resistance rose into the clouds, the actual strength shown was very weak. Thus, the enemy advanced more easily, approaching the Great Wall in one fell swoop, and then occupying Eastern Luan. Now, they have crossed the Luan River to the west, passing through Gubeikou to spy on Miyun, and forcing towards Fengrun in the east. Their surging momentum threatens to shake Tianjin and Beijing and disturb Hebei.

Although our country is poor and our resources are exhausted today, and we have not prepared in advance, we have a large population and a vast land, and the general public has the characteristic of being able to endure hardship, which surpasses all other countries in the world. What we lack is strong leadership and fair and rigorous organization. If our country could fight Japan, we only need to continue to advance fiercely and fight hard. Even if we lose one or two or even three or four provinces due to defeat, there is absolutely nothing to worry about. First, we can take this opportunity to revitalize our country's decadent customs. Second, we can strengthen domestic unity. Third, we can encourage the morale of the whole country. Victory or defeat is common for soldiers. It depends on the final battle and the outcome of the last five minutes. Moreover, Japanese militarists are like the setting sun in terms of historical relations. Although they are very beautiful, their time is not long. In fact, the internal contradictions of their country are gradually unfolding, and with the urging of war, their intensification will be even more rapid. Therefore, even if we make huge sacrifices, we will use this unprecedented price to exert our final strength and engage in a broad and long-term national struggle. We will eventually be able to open up a bright path and gain the final victory.

Judging from the external situation, there are many disputes between countries, and our country seems inevitable to be isolated internationally. However, we must also eliminate dependence and not be discouraged by the bleak future. We must seek self-reliance. Moreover, today's failure lays the foundation for future success. In addition to recognizing the true face of the enemy and striving to fight, we must also encourage the whole country, arouse the masses, and promote the spirit of our 400 million people to strive for self-salvation. We must grieve the failures of the past and plan for the salvation of the future. Our country's existing land still exceeds 25 million square miles, and the accumulation of all natural forces is still twice that of the whole of Europe. Although we are now trapped by the invasion of Japanese capitalists, if our masses can truly awaken, there is still much that can be done. It is not impossible to reverse this decline. May our compatriots actively rise up and sacrifice the individual to exchange for the permanent life of the nation.

Japan Actively Enhances Its Diplomatic and Military Position Against China in the Future

The Departure of Arita and the Appointment of Shigemitsu, a Hardliner, Signifies a Victory for the Hardliners, Who Will Intensify Military Aggression in North China and Force Us to Sign a Peace Treaty

Ugaki, the Governor-General of Korea, Will Return to Tokyo Next Monday, and It Is Expected That There Will Be Changes in the Future of Japanese Politics

(Tokyo) Taking advantage of the resignation of Vice Minister Arita and the vacancy of the Japanese Ambassador to Turkey after Yoshida's death, the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs will change important positions within the ministry. All important positions will be filled by hardliners. The current diplomatic strategy is to abandon the extreme policies towards Europe and the United States and concentrate all efforts on attacking our country. Those who currently wield the real power of Japanese diplomacy are still the military warlords under the Araki faction. Uchida, Shigemitsu, Obata, Tani, and Shiratori are merely willing to be the mouthpieces of the Araki faction. The recent strategy of the Japanese military towards China is simply to force peace through war. It is said that the specific methods are: (1) To intensify the invasion of North China, causing internal divisions in our country, blockading our North China ports by force, and carrying out compulsory trade to remedy its domestic economic panic, eliminate the tide of resistance to Japanese goods, and force our financial and economic situation into an unmanageable situation, thereby coercing our government to sign a treaty of betrayal. (2) To actively provoke the southwestern generals and politicians to oppose the central government, not only preventing the central government from fully responding to the Japanese army but also helping to cause our country's civil war. (China United Press, 16th)

(Tokyo) Foreign Minister Uchida appointed Minister Shigemitsu as Vice Minister Arita's successor because Japanese diplomacy after withdrawing from the League of Nations will focus on the China issue. If China does not reflect and maintain the status quo, the unrest in North China will increase, and peace in East Asia will be worrying. Therefore, in order to create a new Sino-Japanese relationship, Japan needs to actively start activities. Therefore, Foreign Minister Uchida previously placed Ambassador Obata in the position of Foreign Minister's advisor and increased the number of personnel in the Asia Bureau to enhance diplomacy towards China. This time, he reappointed Shigemitsu, making Ambassador Obata, who is proficient in Chinese affairs, and Vice Minister Shigemitsu participate in the hardline faction of Asia Bureau Director Tani and Information Minister Shiratori. So far, Uchida's diplomatic lineup towards China is complete, and only future activities are expected. (Dentsu News Agency, 16th)

(Tokyo) The newly appointed Vice Minister of Foreign Affairs, Shigemitsu Aoi, told someone that he has not yet received the official appointment letter, so he cannot make any announcements. Once appointed, he will definitely serve with one leg. At present, there is no problem other than the leg, and he can do the job. (Dentsu News Agency, 16th)

(Tokyo) Foreign Minister Uchida initially recommended Vice Minister Arita as the ambassador to Turkey, but Arita firmly declined and was dismissed at his request, retiring from the diplomatic world. As a result, the position of ambassador to Turkey will be succeeded by Mushatoji, the minister to Sweden. It is expected that the diplomatic world will take this opportunity to make major changes. (Dentsu News Agency, 16th)

(Tokyo) General Ugaki Kazushige, the Governor-General of Korea, is scheduled to return to Tokyo from Seoul on the 22nd. Although Ugaki's trip is said to be to discuss next year's budget, it is widely believed to be closely related to the future of the political situation. It is still questionable whether Ugaki can succeed Saito in governing, but the current situation has indeed turned in favor of Ugaki. The reasons are as follows: (1) A dozen or so members of the Seiyukai, from the Kuhara and Tokonami factions, secretly gathered somewhere on the afternoon of the 8th and decided to oppose a political coup and oppose Suzuki taking power. The Suzuki faction was very embarrassed upon receiving the news and has sent a leader to persuade Finance Minister Takahashi not to resign. A successor cabinet would be unfavorable to Suzuki and favorable to Ugaki. (2) The financial community and senior officials in the Imperial Court are very wary of Hiranuma, and Hiranuma has no party support. Only the Kokumin Domei is sending overtures, but it cannot have an effect in politics. Ugaki has the support of the Minseito and the anti-Suzuki faction of the Seiyukai, and the Kokumin Domei cannot oppose Ugaki taking power. (3) The hardline faction still dominates the Japanese political situation internally. The forced resignation of Arita, the vice minister of foreign affairs and relative of Seiyukai leader Yamamoto Jotaro, is also evidence of this. (China United Press, 16th)

Araki Reports on the Situation in North China at the Cabinet Meeting

(Tokyo) At the cabinet meeting this morning, Minister of the Army Araki reported on the situation in North China. It is claimed that the purpose of the Japanese army's invasion within the Great Wall this time is nothing more than to consolidate the border between North China and Rehe. (Reuters, 16th)

Disarmament Is at a Critical Juncture

The German Situation Again Causes Tension in Europe and the United States, and Roosevelt Issues a Declaration to Influence the Situation

▲ Reuters, London, 15th: The recent developments in Germany have caused unrest in Europe and the United States. French newspapers speculate that the statements made by German Vice-Chancellor Papen yesterday are a prelude to Hitler's speech in the Reichstag on Wednesday. The extremely conservative French Action Française newspaper said that Papen's words have explained, admitted, and announced the policies that Germany has pursued for the past fifteen years. American confidence in the World Economic Conference has been shaken by German rhetoric on war, the stagnation of the Geneva Disarmament Conference, the possibility of major changes in Danzig, and the ambitions of the Hitler faction in Austria. The British reaction to recent events in Germany can also be seen in the criticism of The Times, which said that before demanding that other countries disarm, it is best to condemn Hitler's main goal of preparing Germany for a war of revenge.

▲ Reuters, Washington, 15th: President Roosevelt will issue a very important declaration on Tuesday, explaining U.S. policy in order to use world public opinion to timely offset the impact of German Chancellor Hitler's speech in the Reichstag on Wednesday. The U.S. President hopes to preserve the Disarmament Conference and pave the way to the World Economic Conference with his declaration. It is expected that this declaration will detail the principles regarding European relations, such as the Monroe Doctrine, but it is also expected that the U.S. President will declare that the United States is prepared to (1) consult with other countries in the event of a danger of war, (2) participate in appropriate security measures, and (3) advocate disarmament in accordance with the scope contained in the plan of British Prime Minister MacDonald.

▲ Reuters, Berlin, 16th: The official document on the German disarmament issue was released today, accusing other countries of trying to undermine the Disarmament Conference on the issue of a unified army system in order to avoid approaching the second point, namely material disarmament, and stating the necessity of Germany's demand for equality. The document compares other countries' active arms race with the fact that German armories are empty, and asks whether it is wise to prematurely acknowledge new responsibilities without making concessions. German Chancellor Hitler will meet with President Hindenburg today, presumably to discuss his important speech in the Reichstag tomorrow with the President.

▲ National Daily, Geneva, 15th: At this time, many representatives to the Disarmament Conference have considered postponing all disarmament discussions to promote the progress of the Economic Conference, but if German Chancellor Hitler insists on promising Germany to rearm, there may be a need to take other procedures. According to several representatives, if Hitler announces after the opening of the Reichstag on Wednesday that Germany is determined to arm its troops (Germany is currently restricted in military strength and some major armaments, so in technical terms it is called disarmed), it is expected that the former Allied powers may individually or jointly submit the matter to the League of Nations Executive Council. However, other representatives believe that there is still an opportunity to break the current deadlock and that the situation will not necessarily reach this extreme. According to news from major financial countries, the uncertainty in the disarmament situation has already had a negative impact on commerce, but there is unlikely to be any progress in the situation before the German Reichstag meets on Wednesday. Hitler has prepared a declaration detailing Germany's attitude on the Disarmament Conference issue, which will be read in the Reichstag and passed, but there is currently no indication whether its content will advise Germany to overstep the provisions of the treaty.

American and British Attitudes

▲ Reuters, Washington, 15th: When Secretary of State Hull was asked today to elaborate on the speech by German Vice-Chancellor Papen and the situation of the Disarmament Conference, Hull's office replied only that it was not appropriate for officials to rush to discuss the matter before it had reached a definite stage. He also said that he had not received Davis' report on the newspaper report that the United Kingdom, the United States, and France had reached a compromise and planned to jointly advise Germany not to act rashly.

▲ Reuters, London, 15th: British Foreign Secretary Simon hopes to personally go to Geneva to represent the British government at the important meeting on Thursday, because the future of the Disarmament Conference depends on this meeting. However, Simon's health is not good. If he cannot bear the fatigue of the journey, he will be represented by Secretary of War Hailsham. Hailsham recently made statements about adopting possible sanctions against Germany, which have provoked a strong response from German Vice-Chancellor Papen.

▲ Reuters, London, 15th: According to recent news, neither Foreign Secretary Simon nor Secretary of War Hailsham plans to go to Geneva on Wednesday. Therefore, Eden, the British representative who is currently in London, will return to Geneva with cabinet instructions to participate in the meeting on Thursday, because Eden has gained the cabinet's full trust in handling all matters as the British representative in Geneva.

▲ Reuters, Geneva, 15th: In view of the precarious fate of the Disarmament Conference, British representative Eden set off for London tonight to report the current situation to the British government. Eden will return to Geneva to participate in the important discussions scheduled for Thursday.

Franco-American Liaison

▲ Havas, Paris, 16th: According to the Daily News, when U.S. representative to the Disarmament Conference Davis met with Foreign Minister Pongue yesterday, Pongue said that Germany had indeed begun to rearm, and various weapons prohibited by the Treaty of Versailles were being manufactured openly. Pongue and Davis seemed to have considered sanctions against this act of violating the treaty. Before the sanctions, or jointly protest to Germany as a warning.

▲ Havas, Paris, 15th: U.S. disarmament representative Davis met with Foreign Minister Pongue at the Ministry of Foreign Affairs for an hour. The topics discussed were particularly the resumption of the Disarmament Conference on Thursday and the World Economic Conference. Regarding the Economic Conference, Davis only asked the French authorities to clarify France's reservations on the tariff truce. Davis had talks in London on the situation created by Germany's recent attitude towards disarmament, seeking to bring the opinions of the United Kingdom and the United States closer on the issue of disarmament. Davis reported the results of his talks to Pongue. Davis also said that Germany's demands for disarmament were of great concern to the United States. He was eager to know the details of Hitler's speech to be delivered in the House of Representatives. He believed that the three democratic countries of the United Kingdom, the United States, and France should unite to cope with the current difficulties. Davis had repeatedly mentioned these points to Pongue. At the general committee meeting on Thursday, it is expected that the representatives of the United Kingdom, France, and the United States will explain the opinions of their respective governments. This declaration must be based on the principles jointly decided by Davis during his recent talks in London and Paris.

▲ Havas, Paris, 15th: After meeting with French Foreign Minister Pongue, U.S. disarmament representative Davis told people that the three issues discussed today were the London World Economic Conference, the Disarmament Conference, and the future events that everyone is waiting for. Regarding the first matter, he said that the situation was quite chaotic. Regarding the Disarmament Conference, the meeting had already stopped. As for future events, he was referring to Hitler's speech to be delivered to the House of Representatives. Davis also said that he was scheduled to go to Geneva on Wednesday evening.

▲ Havas, Geneva, 16th: The foreign ministers of the Little Entente countries held a meeting to exchange views on the progress of the Disarmament Conference and to discuss methods of intervention. The foreign ministers also drafted a procedure for the Economic Conference of the Little Entente countries.

German Situation

▲ Berlin, 15th (National Telegram) German Chancellor Hitler has returned to Berlin from Bavaria. During his weekend vacation, Hitler prepared a speech on German international diplomacy to be delivered in the Reichstag on Wednesday. Many foreign reporters said that all members of the Social Democratic Party would not attend the Reichstag meeting. In fact, this news is not accurate. Not only will they attend the meeting, but they will also join the debate. Ambassador Nadolny, the current German representative to the Disarmament Conference, has also returned from Geneva to Germany and is preparing to participate in various important meetings. Significant developments are expected at that time.

▲ Berlin, 16th (Havas) Nadolny, the chief German representative to the Disarmament Conference, returned to the country to report to the government on the situation of the Disarmament Conference. After Chancellor Hitler delivers a speech in the Reichstag on Wednesday, he will immediately depart for Geneva.

▲ Berlin, 15th (Reuters) The national atmosphere was quite shaken at the end of last week, but now the newspapers are not as concerned about the foreign political situation as before. This is probably because Chancellor Hitler will deliver a speech in the Reichstag on Wednesday to announce Germany's policies. However, the Deutsche Tageszeitung published a lengthy article today stating that war is no longer an issue because no country can benefit from it, and Germany is particularly at risk of being attacked by France and Poland. The article also stated that it would be too uneconomical for the United Kingdom and the United States to engage in such a war, and they would definitely not do so. Although France harbors extravagant hopes of contending for power, it will eventually face retribution for engaging in a war that is without honor or meaning, and it should not be so blind as to be unaware of this.

The Danzig Question

▲ London, 15th (Reuters) During today's meeting of the House of Commons, a request was made to the Foreign Secretary to send a cruiser to Danzig to prevent incidents during the election. The Foreign Secretary replied that he saw no reason to send a ship. He also stated that he had recently met with the senior official stationed in Danzig, who said that the alarming news circulating outside about the possibility of serious disturbances during this election was not credible. After occupying the trade union headquarters, the Danzig National Socialist Party suddenly became moderate. Today, several of its leaders visited the senior official and expressed their willingness to get along with Poland in peace, saying that if the National Socialist Party wins this election, the party's administrative policy will be pro-Polish, ensuring the safety of Polish lives and property, strictly abiding by the existing treaties, and absolutely adhering to the Danzig Constitution guaranteed by the League of Nations.

▲ Danzig, 15th (National Telegram) The leader of the National Socialist Party here, Forster, issued a declaration to the League of Nations' senior official in Danzig, Rosting, today, stating that if the Danzig National Socialist Party takes over the government, it intends to cooperate with the Polish people in peace and will do its best to guarantee the safety of Polish lives and property. The National Socialist Party is determined to maintain the existing treaties and intends to strictly abide by the Constitution guaranteed by the League of Nations. It is reported that the senior official has accepted this declaration and considers it satisfactory.

▲ Geneva, 15th (National Telegram) In recent months, the Free City of Danzig has filed no less than 106 cases with the Council of the League of Nations, complaining about Polish encroachment, all of which are awaiting the Council's decision. This proves the severity of the discord between Danzig and Poland.

▲ Danzig, 16th (National Telegram) The Polish government has recently issued a new order that will greatly impact trade between the Free City of Danzig and Poland. The new order stipulates that from May 15th, goods transported from Danzig to Poland will have to be returned at the border if they are not stamped by Polish customs officials, and even luggage will have to be stamped. The new order was issued suddenly without prior notice, causing great consternation in the Danzig business community.

Roosevelt Will Issue a Declaration Explaining the New U.S. International Policy

No Longer Adopting a Hands-Off Approach to the European Situation, Seeking to Save the Fate of Disarmament and Promote the Success of the Economic Conference

(Paris) After serious developments in the German political situation, it is reported that the U.S. representative, Davis, has told President Roosevelt to immediately issue a declaration stating the importance of the United States directly paying attention to European peace. The U.S. side points to this as a sign that the United States will abandon the Monroe Doctrine and adopt a new international policy. Since yesterday, the situation has completely changed, and the remarks that the United Kingdom and France had already prepared to present at the Geneva Disarmament Conference on Thursday will be greatly revised due to the remarks of the U.S. President today and Hitler tomorrow. It is reported that France approves of the U.S. issuing a moderate declaration to Germany (Reuters, 16th).

(Washington) The deadlock in the Disarmament Conference has a great and profound impact on the Economic Conference, so the anxiety of the U.S. officialdom is even greater than that of the European executives. It is reported that those close to the President expect the U.S. President to issue a broad and passionate declaration, stating the U.S. policy regarding European peace, which is expected to be released around Tuesday. The content is expected to announce the U.S. President's efforts to save the Disarmament Conference in order to promote the success of the Economic Conference. However, there are also those who anticipate that the President will go a step further and request that France and Germany maintain peace. According to private telegrams from the representative stationed in Europe, Davis, Davis advised the President that the United States can no longer take a hands-off policy on the disarmament issue and must clearly state its position. Therefore, those who are generally well-informed expect that the opinions expressed by the U.S. President tonight will be similar to those of the United Kingdom and will have a large part similar to France. It is reported that the U.S. President has studied the issue of imposing sanctions against aggressors and is expected to announce that the United States is willing to fully join the consultation pact proposed by British Prime Minister MacDonald. Those who claim to know the President's attitude even say that the President will support commercial sanctions and not advocate the use of force, at least not willing to use U.S. troops to subdue aggressors. However, if the President's declaration is as expected by some people, openly requesting that France and Germany maintain peace, then the situation must already be very serious, causing the President to believe that the two countries are on the verge of open rupture. According to reports received by the White House and the State Department, all of Europe is currently in suspicion and has a tendency to split into two major factions: Italy, Germany, and Austria form one faction and receive assistance from Austria. They observe every move of France, Poland, and their allies with suspicion. Conversely, France, Poland, and the Little Entente oppose all actions to revise the peace treaty. Among the major powers, only the United Kingdom and the United States are not shrouded in this atmosphere of suspicion. If this situation continues, the World Economic Conference will have little hope of complete success. Therefore, the United States has a need to come up with a plan to save the situation. It is now expected that when the U.S. President issues a declaration, what he agreed with British Prime Minister MacDonald a few days ago can also be released, and the State Department has already stated that the United States does not approve of Germany's large-scale rearmament (National Telegram, 15th).

(Washington) Today, U.S. President Roosevelt assumed the role of world leader, inviting all countries to guarantee not to send armed forces across borders and requesting the entire world to accept British Prime Minister MacDonald's disarmament proposal. In this declaration of the U.S. policy on European peace, the U.S. President also warned the world that in this time of crisis, if any strong country refuses to clearly register its opposition to aggressive behavior, then the world will know who is to blame for the disasters that will befall. I urge all countries not to bear this responsibility. The U.S. President subsequently urged all countries to accept British Prime Minister MacDonald's disarmament plan as the first step towards avoiding war, as the plan will substantially reduce aggressive weapons and establish a consultation system that can bring together countries to seek remedies when world peace is threatened. In addition, the U.S. President also proposed that while starting the machinery to make the world accept the British plan, existing troops and armaments should not be increased, and countries should solemnly guarantee not to increase their war-making tools. The Americans have always been determined to refuse to be bound by consultation agreements. This declaration by the U.S. President is a sign of a major change in U.S. foreign policy (National Telegram, 15th).

Major Reorganization of the U.S. Navy

One-Third of Warships Will Rotate on Leave, and All Will Be Deployed in Formations After Three Years

(Preparation for the Pacific War)

(Washington) Today, U.S. Navy Commander-in-Chief Rear Admiral Blythe ordered that one-third of warships be withdrawn from the fleet as reserve ships starting July 1st, and announced that the number of naval personnel will also be reduced by 2,000. Senior naval officers were surprised by this news, believing that if one-third of the warships are placed in idleness, they will not be able to maintain proper effectiveness. However, Blythe said that the ships will be rotated on leave, which will not affect the effectiveness of the navy. It is now determined that the ships to be withdrawn from the fleet on July 1st include five battleships, five heavy cruisers, three light cruisers, thirty-three destroyers, sixteen submarines, one aircraft carrier, and two light mine-laying boats. These warships will be idle for six months before being redeployed into the fleet to replace other ships. This rotation will continue until January 1, 1936, when all warships will be redeployed in formations. In the next two and a half years, the number of ships in formation will be only ten battleships, ten heavy cruisers, seven light cruisers, sixty destroyers, and some submarines and aircraft carriers. However, according to this plan, in case of emergency, the idle ships can still be immediately deployed into the fleet because each ship only rests for six months out of ten months and is repaired in docks during the rest period. They can still be deployed at any time when needed, so there is actually not much loss in naval effectiveness. The naval airship Macon is not included in the rotation and will always be deployed in the fleet (National Telegram, 15th).

German Railcar

Travels at 100 Miles Per Hour

(Berlin, 15th, National Telegram) Today, the fastest train in continental Europe, the Hamburg Flyer between Berlin and Hamburg, carried 78 passengers, including several Chinese engineers, during its trial run today. The journey from Berlin to Hamburg took only two hours and eighteen minutes, saving about one hour compared to ordinary express trains. The return journey departed from Hamburg at 3:20 PM and arrived in Berlin at 5:36 PM. This train reaches 100 miles per hour when running at speed.

The Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission Formulates Five Measures for Tibet

(2) Telegraph the Dalai Lama to stop military action. Chen Cheng Telegraphs About Bandit Situation

(Nanjing) Chen Cheng telegraphed to Nanjing on the 16th, reporting on the bandit situation recently detected: In order to protect spring farming and seek food, the bandits want to retreat but cannot. Their main force is now gathered between Yile. Many officers and soldiers of the bandit army have come to surrender. It is said that: (1) There is talk of the fake central government moving its capital. The fake general hospital is in Ningdu, and the fake temporary hospitals and supply stations are being moved. (2) The bandit area recently issued 600,000 and 800,000 public bonds in two phases, forcing the bandit people to buy them, but they cannot be used or offset against rent. (3) The foreign soldiers in the bandit army are very willing to surrender. (4) The casualties in the Dongpo, Huangbo, and Lean campaigns were very heavy. They are now forcibly conscripting men in various counties to serve. New recruits account for 70-80% of each army corps. Women are already used for farming and guarding in the bandit area. (5) Mao Zedong is seriously ill and is recuperating in the rear. Peng Dehuai has not been seen since the defeat in Lean, etc. (Special Dispatch, 16th).

Ministry of Industry Stipulates Provisional Measures for Trademark Registration

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Industry has formulated the following provisional measures for the Ministry and the Trademark Bureau to receive company establishment registration documents: (1) In order to facilitate the application for establishment registration by various companies, they may directly send the application to the Ministry or send it to the Ministry's Trademark Bureau for collection and transfer to the Ministry. (2) After the Ministry receives the above-mentioned documents, it will still order the relevant local competent authorities to review them. However, when obstacles occur in the location of the company and the competent authorities cannot exercise their functions according to law, the Ministry may temporarily handle the case directly. (3) The office expenses stipulated in Article 16 of the Company Registration Rules shall be issued by the Ministry to the local competent authorities upon approval of the registration, but those handled in accordance with the provisions of the preceding article may be transferred to the office expenses of the receiving agency (Central News Agency, 16th).

Hui Muslims Capture Kashgar

(Peiping) This place received news today that on May 2nd, Hui Muslims in Aksu, Xinjiang, suddenly attacked and captured the old city of Kashgar. The new city also fell the next day. Many Han Chinese took refuge in the city's Taoist Yin government office, but were not attacked. Indian merchants and Swedish missionaries took refuge in the British consulate, but no foreigners were disturbed. However, the new city of Jiayierqiang has fallen into the hands of Hui Muslims. Several Swedish missionaries there were arrested and ordered by the Hui Muslim leader to leave the country within eight days. It is also reported that an incident occurred in Yangjihase (transliteration) south of Kashgar. The British people and industries there have not been disturbed (Reuters, 16th).

(Shantou) Shantou Tongyuzhuang Bank continued to collapse. Various banks have successively mortgaged real estate to the Provincial China and other banks for turnover. The provincial government ordered Shantou to strictly prohibit the export of silver. The Chao'an Bank Joint Guarantee issued 450,000 yuan in white bills, and the Shantou Banking Industry White Bill Joint Guarantee Regulations were announced (Special Dispatch, 16th).

The Amoy Jiantan Steamer Robbed

(Amoy) The Amoy Taili Company’s Jiantan steamer, on the 14th, was returning to Amoy from Dongshan. At night, pirates appeared on the ship. Six pirates suddenly emerged and shot at the helmsman, missing. They robbed over ten thousand yuan and six guard guns, forcing the ship to sail to the Gongkou Bay of Zhao'an, where they disembarked. On the morning of the 15th, the ship returned to Dongshan to report the crime. No one was injured or kidnapped. (16th Special Dispatch)
