China Merchants Steam Navigation Company (CMSNC) to Take Over the Yangzi Wharf Tomorrow

Extensive Repairs Will Be Carried Out After the Takeover

And the Head of the Chinese Warehouse is Designated to Manage It Concurrently

The Yangzi Wharf in Pudong, after the Ministry of Communications negotiated with the Japanese-owned Haiyang Society to recover it, the CMSNC petitioned to be assigned to manage it. The Ministry approved the petition and scheduled the takeover for tomorrow, incorporating it into the Chinese Warehouse. The details are as follows:

Ministry Order Assigns it to CMSNC

The Yangzi Wharf occupies 43 mu of land, with a wharf length of 550 feet and eight warehouses. After the Ministry of Communications negotiated with the Japanese-owned Haiyang Society for its recovery, the Navigation Administration Bureau temporarily took custody of it. Since the CMSNC was nationalized and after the Board of Directors petitioned the Ministry of Communications to assign the wharf to the company's management, the Ministry sent Gao Tingzi, the Director of the Navigation Administration Department, to Shanghai to negotiate. The day before yesterday, the CMSNC received a Ministry order approving the assignment. At the same time, the Navigation Administration Bureau also received a Ministry order to hand it over.

Handover and Receiving Personnel

Liu Hongsheng, the General Manager of the CMSNC, appointed Jin Duo, the Head of the Warehouse Affairs Section, and Jin Xin'san, the Head of the Chinese Warehouse, as receiving officers. After the takeover, it will be incorporated into the Chinese Warehouse and managed concurrently by Jin Xin'san, the Head of the Chinese Warehouse. At the same time, Zhu Yaoting, the Director of the Navigation Administration Bureau, appointed Chen Yici, the Head of the First Section, and Qin Jiyun, the Director of the Custody Office, as handover officers. They immediately rushed to prepare an inventory to facilitate the handover.

Decision to Take Over Tomorrow

Jin Duo and Jin Xin'san, the receiving officers from the CMSNC, contacted Chen Yici and Qin Jiyun, the handover officers from the Navigation Administration Bureau, the day before yesterday afternoon at 2 p.m. to discuss the handover procedures. It was decided that after the Navigation Administration Bureau completed the inventory, they would notify the CMSNC by telephone to determine the handover date. A reporter from the Xin Sheng News Agency interviewed Qin Jiyun last night, who stated that after receiving the order, they immediately rushed to prepare the inventory, which would be completed by the 17th, and the handover was scheduled for the 18th. A formal notification will be sent to the CMSNC tomorrow (i.e., today). The warehouse keeper who manages the warehouses will also be handed over.

Plans to Hire Workers for Repairs

The CMSNC considers the Yangzi Wharf to be dilapidated and in need of repair due to years of neglect. It has decided to hire workers for repairs immediately after the takeover and to demolish the wall separating it from the Chinese Warehouse to facilitate integration.

Ministry of Communications Orders a Large Batch of Telegraph Machines from England

Worth 12,000 Pounds

Expected to Arrive in Two Months

Xin Xin News Agency reports that the telegraph machines used by various telegraph offices in China are mostly of the Morse and Weston types. Although these machines have high transmission speeds, re-punching telegrams on paper is slow. Recently, most countries have adopted the British Creed high-speed telegraph machine, which eliminates the re-punching step during transmission. Recognizing this, the Ministry of Communications has ordered seven machines from England, worth 12,000 gold pounds. They are expected to arrive in about two months and will be deployed to telegraph offices in Nanjing, Shanghai, Hankou, Tianjin, Beiping, Qingdao, and Yantai.

Progress of the Fisheries Improvement Association

Established Ten District Offices to Collect Taxes and Now Sends Warships to Cruise in the Open Sea

The Jiangzhe District Fisheries Construction Fee Collection Office of the Fisheries Improvement Committee has been actively carrying out fisheries construction and improvement plans since its establishment. A reporter from Xin Xin News Agency interviewed Dai Yongtang, the Director of the office, yesterday and inquired about everything. He was kind enough to provide detailed information, which is recorded below:

Establishment of District Offices

The office manages the Jiangzhe region. Due to the vast area under its jurisdiction, management is difficult to cover. Therefore, it is divided into ten districts to handle affairs. Each district has a director who oversees the collection of construction fees and other matters within the district. (1) Ding Shen District, Director Wang Zhiliang; (2) Ning Zhen District, Director Cai Sheng; (3) Ning Xiangnan District, Director Wu Yichen; (4) Wen Tai District, concurrently managed by the third district; (5) Songhu District, concurrently managed by the head office; (6) Hang Jia Shao District, Director Wu Weinan; (7) Hu Tai Su District, Director Liu Tongyu; (8) Chongtong District, Director Gu Jiacai; (9) Haizhou District, concurrently managed by the eighth district; (10) Jing Chang District, Director Shen Zefei. The ten district directors have been appointed and have taken up their posts in their respective districts.

Collection in Various Districts

The office collects taxes on five types of fish: (1) fresh fish; (2) salted fish; (3) dried fish; (4) marinated fish; (5) shellfish. The collection standard is one percent. According to reports from the Directors of Ding Shen District, Chongtong District, Hu Tai Su District, Haizhou District, Hang Jia Shao District, and Wen Tai District, collection has begun and is proceeding smoothly. Ning Zhen District has not yet started collecting. No reports have been received from the other districts, and orders have been sent to urge them separately. Currently, the ice-fresh industries have unanimously approved the construction fee. Only the Shipu barrel fish merchants are still objecting, but this is a minor issue and has no bearing on the future of the office.

Sending Warships to Cruise

For the sake of maintaining the safety of fishermen and merchants, the office has consulted with the Fisheries Administration Bureau and sent warships to patrol the open sea. The Hai Lan warship has been dispatched to the Ning Zhen area, the Hai Hong warship to the Chongming Qidong Haizhou area, the Fu Hai warship to the Ding Shen area, the Qing An warship also departed yesterday evening to the Ning Zhen area, and the Hai Gu warship has been dispatched to cruise the Shengshan Daishan Ma Ji area.

Improvement Plans

Chen Gongbo, the Minister of Industry, and Chen Zhongsheng, the Director of the Fisheries Administration Bureau, have drafted improvement plans. The contents are: (1) to organize a fisheries bank; (2) to organize fishermen's lending offices. When fishermen's fishing businesses are limited by financial difficulties and cannot develop, measures will be taken to support them, and loans will be provided by the bank and lending offices according to the circumstances; (3) to establish coastal meteorological stations to report marine weather. In the event of hurricanes or other changes involving danger, preventive measures can be taken in advance; (4) to establish radio stations to report fisheries market conditions and other information.

Sculpted by Yang Hui of the Tang Dynasty

Dispute over the Statue of a Child Goddess Fraud Case

Authenticated by Archaeologists as a Rare Treasure, Stored by Zhang Youquan Awaiting a Good Price

丨An Wenpu Fraudulently Sold the Statue and Falsely Accused the Owner of Kidnapping丨

丨An was Recently Arrested for Another Case, and the Owner Has Also Filed a Lawsuit丨

An Wenpu from Beiping suddenly went to Hong Kong from Shanghai in March of this year, posing as a major antique merchant. He defrauded two antique shops, Baoyuanzhai and Jiefa Zhan, in Hong Kong of an ivory vase and two ancient paintings. He took them back to Shanghai and sold them to antique shops such as Yibaozhai on Tongfu Road. Later, after the Hong Kong authorities received a report from the victims, they telegraphed the Shanghai Public Concession police authorities to investigate and arrest the major fraudster. Before he could be extradited to Hong Kong, he committed another crime in the French Concession. The Second Special District Court took him from the First Special District Court for interrogation and confirmed the facts. He has now been sentenced to imprisonment and confined in prison. However, it was recently discovered that An Wenpu had also defrauded Zhang Youquan from Sichuan of a

Tang Dynasty Statue of a Child Goddess

This item is a rare treasure. The details of his fraudulent activities are as follows: Yang Hui of the Tang Dynasty was a famous sculptor. His clay statues are now rare. Zhang Youquan from Sichuan possessed a statue of a child goddess that had been authenticated by archaeologists as indeed being the work of Yang Hui. Because Yang's sculptures have become highly valued in recent years, Zhang brought the statue to Shanghai this spring to sell it. At that time, Wenpu was also in Shanghai. Through an introduction, they became acquainted. Wenpu claimed to have a "Binpu Antique Foreign Goods Company" in Beiping. Zhang felt that he had a good understanding of antiques, so he gave him the statue to examine. Wenpu praised it repeatedly and took it upon himself to sell it. Zhang then entrusted the statue to him to sell on consignment. After ten days, Wenpu said that

A Westerner Wished to Buy it

He invited Zhang to negotiate the price with the Westerner. Unexpectedly, the Westerner only offered 2,000 yuan. Zhang did not want to sell it cheaply and took the statue back. Soon after, he received a telegram and hurried back to Sichuan. He entrusted the statue to his daughter, Zhang Yunhe, and son-in-law, Wu Xi'an, instructing them that if they received a reasonable price, they could sell it. Not long after Zhang returned to Sichuan, An Wenpu again asked Wu for the statue, saying that a customer wanted to buy it. Since Wu knew An well, he gave him the statue, agreeing to decide in three days. When the time came, An neither responded nor returned the statue. Wu urged him to return it, but he made excuses and delayed. From then on, the statue was in An's possession. After more than a month, An disappeared from Shanghai, having someone spread the word that he had taken a

Westerner to Japan with the Statue

To Tokyo, awaiting a good price before reporting back. Wu was helpless. It was not until August 24th of last year that he learned that An had returned to Shanghai and was staying at Room 415 of the Great China Hotel in the racecourse. Wu, his wife, and a friend immediately went to see him and inquired about the whereabouts of the statue. An was evasive. When Wu's tone became stern, fearing that his scheme would be exposed, he wrote a note, with his friend Jin Shaolu as guarantor, promising to sell it within three months or return the original item, otherwise he would pay 10,000 yuan. After signing the note, An changed rooms every day. Every time he met with Wu, he did not give his real address, and his whereabouts were extremely secretive. Around mid-October, as the agreed deadline approached, Wu suddenly heard people say that An had long ago

Sold it for a Good Price and Spent the Money

The note was just a way to delay, and he would make a fake statue to return within the deadline. Wu was shocked and asked his cousin, Xu Bokui, to help him watch An's movements. On the morning of November 22nd, Wu received a call from Xu, informing him that An had gone to Xu's house. Wu rushed to 6 Guanhua Lane, Lafayette Road, to meet with Xu and An. Xu said that An had decided to bring other antiques of equal value to the statue as collateral. But Wu waited until sunset, and An's brother, An Wenbin, still came empty-handed. When asked about the antiques to be used as collateral, he said they would be delivered at 9 p.m. After saying this, he left. Until midnight, Wenbin suddenly led the French Concession

A Large Number of Armed Detectives

They swarmed into the house, accusing Xu of being a kidnapper. Wu explained the situation. An Wenpu then accused Wu of being a ticket-watcher. Xu, Wu, and their friends were all arrested. After several trials by the Second Special District Court and the High Third Branch Court, the truth was revealed, and Xu and others were found innocent. However, the lawsuit ended, and An Wenpu's whereabouts were unknown. The statue was still difficult to recover. This spring, An's fraud case in Hong Kong was exposed. Wu only then learned of his whereabouts and was about to report him to the police. He happened to have secretly returned to Shanghai, throwing himself into the net. He was detained by the French Concession police for another case and sent to the Second Special Court for punishment. Wu Xi'an has now hired lawyer Shen Yuesheng to file a suit in the First Special Court, claiming 10,000 yuan for the statue. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Shen Hong presided over the trial. Because the defendant was imprisoned in the French Concession prison and had yet to be transferred, Judge Shen ordered a postponement for another hearing.

Massive Export of Plough Cattle to Aid the Enemy

Recently, many ships carrying plough cattle for sale in Shanghai have been entering Wusong. There are one or two or three or four ships every day. Yesterday, there were even more, with a total of five ships in one day, each carrying twenty or thirty or forty or fifty cattle. The cattle are transported from various ports in Jiangbei. The ships are mostly Jiangbei sandboats disguised as carrying fresh pigs to avoid attracting attention. It is said that these plough cattle are all sold in Shanghai to a certain country as food needed for military rations, so the profit is very high. However, the sale of plough cattle is prohibited by law, so in the past, most cattle dealers smuggled them at night. It is said that now, because a certain official with real power over the water transport is handling the transport, shipowners are acting openly and brazenly. According to Jiangbei people, these people only care about huge profits and disregard the great impact on farmers' cultivation in the future, which is very hateful.

A Badger Eating People in Luodian

A Girl Had Her Foot Bitten Off

Water and Fire Were Used to Capture One

Shenjia Archway, about three miles southwest of Luodian Town in Baoshan County, is behind Shenjia Cemetery. The day before yesterday evening, an eight-year-old girl named Shen from a local farmer was playing in the fields when she was dragged by a badger from the cemetery to the entrance of a grave, where it bit off her foot. It is said that because the entrance of the hole was narrow, it could not be dragged in, otherwise her life would have been in danger. Currently, the girl has been sent to the hospital for treatment. The villagers burned the badger in the cemetery with torches and poured water into the hole, capturing one weighing more than 170 kilograms.

Phone Price Hikes in the Chinese District Seem Inevitable

In response to the case, a letter was received from 46 trade associations, including the restaurant and food industry, jointly requesting that telephone fees not be increased until the industry and commerce in the Chinese area have recovered. This is a request that is truly unavoidable. The circumstances are being reiterated, and it is hoped that they will be considered and approved. It is noted that the Shanghai Silk Cotton Weaving Trade Association and others have submitted a report that includes a directive from the Ministry of Communications, which states that the Shanghai Telephone Bureau is adapting to local needs and increasing the efficiency of calls by refitting automatic telephone exchanges. The cost of the necessary machinery and materials is estimated at 3 million yuan. The cost of the machinery and materials will be paid in installments. In addition to the portion paid by the Ministry at the time of ordering, according to the machine purchase contract, the bureau will have to pay 4,000 to 8,000 U.S. dollars per month from the date of completion of the main exchange. There are more than 2,200 telephone subscribers in the north and south of Shanghai. The original rental income is only enough for routine maintenance. As for paying for the machinery and materials, there is no way to do so. The Ministry is unable to provide funds at this time of financial difficulty, and the merchants in the area have not yet recovered from the January 28th Incident, so some consideration must be given. Therefore, as a last resort, the rental fees for each household will be slightly increased to make up for it. This will not be enough to pay for the machinery and materials, and other methods must be devised. The facts are there, and they should be known to the merchants in Shanghai. In addition, the Shanghai Telephone Bureau's refitting of automatic telephone exchanges has the same call efficiency as telephones in the concessions, but the rental fees charged are lower than those in the concessions. This shows that the Ministry has been considerate of the merchants' difficulties to the utmost. As for the statement that the number of employees will be reduced and consumption will be saved after the automatic exchanges are refitted, the bureau is now adding a manual switchboard to the bureau to facilitate communication between users in the Chinese and concession areas, dispatching personnel and dividing shifts for duty, specializing in connection. There is little reduction in the number of employees, and the increase in debt has exceeded the original routine budget by more than two times. The trade associations are all composed of merchants, and they must have a thorough understanding of business principles. They must carefully consider this, pay according to regulations, and the request to stop the Shanghai Telephone Bureau from raising prices should not be considered. A Ministry order has been issued for investigation and record. After verification, the Ministry's approval is very detailed, and the request from the restaurant and food industry trade associations for a temporary exemption cannot be granted. The corresponding letter is being sent in response. Please investigate and inform the trade associations to carefully consider the instructions and pay according to regulations. This is truly a matter of public interest. Respectfully addressed to the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce.

Steamboat Workers Union Telegraphs to Investigate and Punish Road Workers Who Caused the Accident

The Shanghai Inland River Steamboat Workers Union sent a telegram to the Construction Department of the Jiangsu Provincial Government, saying: "Director of the Construction Department of the Jiangsu Provincial Government in Zhenjiang, according to a letter from member Xin Da Wheel, veteran Lian Guo Yu, veteran Lian Bing Gen, on the 10th of this month at 1:00 p.m., en route from Suzhou to Shengze via Bei Di Nan Shou, a barge of workers from the Su Jia Road, forcibly wanted to be towed to Pingwang. The veterans and others politely refused because the boat was rotten and feared it could not be towed. The workers were unreasonable and aggressive. At the time, they were forced to comply. When passing Shuang Tingzi, as expected, the boat cracked and took on water and sank. The veterans and others, being responsible, immediately stopped the steamboat, assisted in rescue, and a worker named Chen reported to the Pingwang Su Jia Road Engineering Office together with the veterans. The workers claimed to have lost four stones of rice. The Engineering Office advised the steamboat to pay two stones of rice as a peaceful settlement. Unexpectedly, yesterday when returning to Bei Di, the worker named Chen suddenly gathered seventy or eighty people, forcing the veterans to pay compensation, threatening violence. Fortunately, the defense corps of the office suppressed the incident. The matter has not yet been resolved. We believe that it is common for road workers to gather crowds to commit violence. In this case, the veterans repeatedly refused to tow the boat to avoid danger. When forced to tow, they extorted money. In summary, their behavior is extremely absurd. The veterans and others' personal losses are small, but they are hindering traffic and disturbing travelers. If this is not strictly warned against, human rights will not be guaranteed. In addition to reporting to the bureau and forwarding a letter to the trade association requesting the Jiangsu Provincial Construction Department to thoroughly investigate, we are reporting the situation. Based on this, we believe that road workers causing trouble by extorting money has been reported many times. This time, gathering crowds to extort money is clear evidence. There are many small boats entering and leaving the waterway. If this is not investigated, it will affect traffic. We are urgently telegraphing to you, requesting a quick investigation and punishment, dismissing the worker named Chen from his post and punishing him according to the law to ensure safe navigation and protect human rights. We are telegraphing anxiously, awaiting your order, Shanghai Inland River Steamboat Workers Union, Standing Directors Zhang Jinhua, Yu Jirong, Wan Wenqing, all bow down."

The Chinese Child Welfare Association has recently received letters from various sectors advocating for humanitarianism, reporting on underage girls who have been sold or forced into prostitution on the streets, in hotels, and in various game fields in the concessions. This not only infringes on their freedom but also harms their bodies. The association has always paid close attention to this and has already rescued many child prostitutes through the protection department, allowing them to escape from the fire pit. Now, it has gained the sympathy of people from all walks of life. In addition to formulating concrete measures, it is first writing to the concession authorities to request that they take steps to ban and investigate the following: "Respectfully, Shanghai is a place where people from all over the world gather, and there are good and bad people. When the moon is white and the lights are red, underage girls who have been sold or forced into prostitution, whether coerced by pimps or seduced by fortune tellers, fill the markets, constantly enticing people. The young masters and frivolous idlers, disregarding shame and humanity, flock to them. This phenomenon greatly hinders public order and good morals. Moreover, these child prostitutes have shallow knowledge and incomplete development and are mostly abducted from various places, either by force or by sale. They are oppressed by the environment and abused by the unlawful. It is not their wish, and their situation is pitiful. As a result, they are thin and have a variety of diseases. If measures are not taken to strictly prohibit this, it will harm society and destroy humanity. It is not a small matter. The association is responsible for child welfare and cannot bear to see these underage girls fall into the dust and be trampled upon. Therefore, we are writing to request that your police station investigate and strictly prohibit this in order to maintain morality."

New Vault at the Reclamation Bank

The China Reclamation Bank has been constructing a new eight-story building on its own land at the intersection of Beijing Road and Jiangxi Road for more than a year, and it is nearing completion. The sturdiness of the vault's construction and the perfection of its equipment are particularly noteworthy. It is understood that the vault door, safe deposit boxes, and all equipment were planned and supplied by the Mosler Safe Company of the United States, and a renowned American engineer specially dispatched by the Shanghai Shenchang & Co., Ltd. supervised the installation. The vault is surrounded by 20-inch-thick reinforced concrete walls, with extra-thick steel plates installed inside, making it exceptionally strong. The entire vault is located on the second floor, which is high and dry, unlike those located in the basement. The steel plate of the vault door is more than ten inches thick and has a four-layer structure, consisting of various fire-resistant and anti-theft materials. The door is equipped with an extremely complex combination lock that can be changed up to 100,000,000 times. Even skilled craftsmen with the key would find it difficult to open without authorization from the responsible personnel. The vault is equipped with an alarm bell; if the vault wall is disturbed in the slightest, the alarm will automatically sound, alerting the outside. In addition, the interior is equipped with an air extraction door and high-speed electric fans to facilitate air circulation. The entire vault area is spacious and equipped with thousands of Mosler standard safe deposit boxes of various sizes. Each box is equipped with a Mosler-invented double-nosed lock that can be changed eight million times. Once a tenant terminates the lease, the mechanism is immediately changed, making it impossible to open even with the original key in hand. These are all characteristics of the new vault. Moreover, the rental price is particularly low, so many people have already made reservations in recent days.

Zhang Zhendong, Who Was Electrocuted to Death in a Thunderstorm the Other Day

Hair Charred and Sulfur Smell Pervades

Judge Confirms Death by Electrocution

The weather the other day was unusually sultry. By 3 p.m., dark clouds gathered, and the sky turned dim. Before long, a torrential rain poured down, and flashes of lightning and deafening thunderclaps occurred simultaneously. After about half an hour, the shower stopped. However, while the lightning and thunder were raging, a man was struck and killed by lightning on the open space west of the Seventh District, Second Precinct Police Station on the north side of Yixiang Road in Pudong. After the rain stopped, the incident caused a sensation in the neighborhood. People who went to see the victim found that his hair was charred and a sulfur smell permeated the air. After an investigation by the police station, the man was identified as Zhang Zhendong, 23 years old, from Hubei Province. He worked as a mud carrier in the Xiehe Company, and his home was in a nearby shack. When the family was notified and questioned, they claimed that they did not know why the deceased had gone to that place, resulting in his death by lightning. Since the death occurred on the road, the police district ordered Chen Jinsheng, the land guard of the Twenty-third Bao Sixth Tu, to report the case to the District Court for examination. Prosecutor Wu and others, commissioned by the court, arrived at the scene and confirmed that the death was caused by electrocution. They ordered the family to take the body for burial.

Publication of the Second Volume, Ninth Issue of the "Shen Bao Monthly"

The second volume, ninth issue of the "Shen Bao Monthly" was published on the 15th of this month. Liu Mingzhu's Divorce Appeal Still Rejected

Liu Mingzhu, the daughter of Liu Huizhi, the general manager of the China Industrial Bank, requested a divorce from her husband, Duan Ao, from the Second Special Court on the grounds that he suffered from mental illness. However, Duan claimed that the allegations were untrue and hired lawyer Dong Yu to write a defense. After the first instance trial, the court rejected the plaintiff's claim. However, Liu was not satisfied and appealed to the Third Branch of the High Court. A hearing was held once last month. Since both parties were absent at that time, the hearing was rescheduled to continue the afternoon before yesterday. On that day, the appellant Liu Mingzhu arrived in court with lawyer Lu, while the appellee Duan Ao did not appear and was represented by lawyer Dong. The judge first questioned Duan and Liu, and Liu testified that her husband suffered from mental illness and beat people indiscriminately, injuring many. She feared that there was no hope of treatment, so she came to request a divorce. Then, lawyer Dong stood up and argued that Duan Ao was appointed as a military translator by Commander-in-Chief Chiang Kai-shek of the National Government in 1929, as evidenced by the letter of appointment (presented to the court at the time). This proved that Duan had no mental illness. Moreover, the appellant's claim that Duan had beaten people was entirely unfounded and had no supporting evidence, making it difficult to believe. Finally, the court declared the debate closed and announced its verdict yesterday afternoon, rejecting Liu's appeal.

Continued Hearing on the Case of Huang Jiuzhitang's Mis-Prescription

The Huang Jiuzhitang pharmacy on Zhejiang Road, south of Touji Bridge, had previously dispensed medicine for Weng Xieyao, the chief auditor of the Tianchan Theater. However, it was discovered that four ingredients were missing from the prescription by Dr. Zhang Peizhi, who was treating Weng's wife. He immediately sent someone to the pharmacy to make up for the missing ingredients. Unexpectedly, they replaced "Huangqin" (Scutellaria baicalensis) with North American ginseng. This mistake was repeated, treating life as a child's play. When Weng confronted them, they stubbornly defended themselves. Therefore, he took the shop's accountant, Zhou Zilin, to the Lao Zha Police Station. After being questioned by the police chief, he was ordered to file a private prosecution in the court. He then hired a lawyer to file a criminal lawsuit against Cai Maohuai and Zhou Zilin, the assistant managers of Huang Jiuzhitang, for dereliction of duty. A hearing had been held once before, as reported in this newspaper. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Liu Yugui continued the hearing, and Dr. Zhang testified that the four missing medicines from Huang Jiuzhitang the first time were the most important ones. Although they later made up for the ingredients according to the prescription, they actually used Huangqin to replace North American ginseng, which was even more absurd. The properties of Huangqin and North American ginseng are completely different. Taking Huangqin would cause abdominal pain for the patient. Fortunately, it was discovered before the medicine was taken, and no disaster occurred. When questioned, the accused completely shifted the responsibility to Tang Wenkui alone, claiming that Tang dispensed the medicine and that Tang was a temporary worker in the shop who had left the shop on April 12 and his whereabouts were unknown. Judge Liu ordered a rescheduled hearing for the afternoon of May 29.

The Case of Wu Jingxiong's Chauffeur's Tragic Death

丨Russian Chauffeur Sentenced丨

Zhang A'wang, a 51-year-old man from Ningbo who worked as a chauffeur for Wu Jingxiong, was on his way home on a bicycle at around 10 p.m. on the 10th of this month after finishing his work. While passing through the intersection of Avenue Joffre and Dixifeng Road, he was suddenly run over by a Russian chauffeur named Stan Gremlin, driving public bus No. 15103, on the sidewalk, killing him. The Jing'an Temple Police Station sent the body to the Philander Road Morgue for examination. Prosecutor Guo, commissioned by the First Special Court, arrived at the morgue for examination and, considering that the Russian driver was suspected of negligence, ordered the police station to file a public prosecution according to law, as previously reported. The court had already concluded a hearing once. Yesterday morning, it was time for the verdict to be announced. Judge Huang Risheng took the stand in the Eighth Criminal Court and pronounced the judgment. The main text was that the Russian Stan Gremlin was guilty of causing death through negligence in his work and was sentenced to one year and six months of imprisonment. The incidental civil suit was transferred to the Civil Court for trial.

A Boatman's Foot Crushed

Leaving the Gate, He Couldn't Escape Disaster

Neighboring Boat Tried to Rescue Jinbao

Chen Zhanglin's kiln cargo boat, fully loaded with bricks and tiles from Zhejiang Province, was sailing on the South Huangpu River near the Shanghai Cement Factory yesterday morning when it stopped due to the rising tide and adverse current. Chen went ashore to buy goods, while two boatmen were on board to watch over the boat. One of them, named Jinbao, was sitting on the side of the bow washing clothes when a boat leaving the gate, fully loaded with flour, sailed southward quickly with the current. Due to a slight delay in turning the rudder, it directly collided with Chen's boat. Jinbao was unable to avoid it, and his feet were crushed, causing him to fall into the river in extreme pain. Seeing the accident, the other boat sped south and fled. Fortunately, Yang Hesheng from a neighboring boat saw it and went forward to rescue Jinbao, immediately taking Jinbao to the hospital. He also found Chen and informed him of the situation. Chen hired a small boat to chase south and, it was reported that he had chased the boat to the south of Dujiahang in the afternoon, apprehended the boat, and taken the boat owner to the police district for investigation. As for Jinbao, his feet were crushed, and it was said that one foot was crushed and the bone was shattered, and that he might be disabled.

At the Same Time, an Exhibition of Children's Happiness Will Be Held

The Zhuanqiao Farmers' Education Center in this county, recognizing that villagers lack parenting knowledge and neglect hygiene, decided to hold the first Small Village Folk Music Festival on May 22 in Zhuanqiao, Shanghai-Minhang Road, to promote these issues. In addition to hiring experts to guide parenting methods and examine the children's health, there will also be a children's happiness exhibition, children's instinct activities, promoting human health, and promoting the spirit of the nation. Small martial artists will perform martial arts, small musicians will perform music, and Guangyi Society will perform "Little Heroes" and "Gua Gua Gua" to entertain the villagers. The day coincides with the Farming Festival, and the center will hold a Farming Ceremony at 10 a.m., inviting agricultural experts to give lectures. The director of the center, Zhang Yi, has been contacting various sectors since today, and it is expected that there will be a grand occasion at that time.

Advocating That the National Labor Representatives Should Be Elected by the Labor Sector

The Shanghai Workers' Aircraft Fundraising Extended for One Month to End

The Shanghai Federation of Trade Unions convened an extraordinary representative congress of all trade unions in the city at the union's location on Fuyou Road yesterday afternoon. More than 100 representatives from more than 60 trade unions attended. The presidium, nominated by the Federation of Trade Unions, consisted of Zhu Xuefan, Zhou Xuexiang, and Li Mengnan. After the ceremony was held according to etiquette, Zhu Xuefan reported, and then the discussion began. (2) The case that the Shanghai Workers' Aircraft should actively raise funds was resolved and extended for one month until June 15, when the final conclusion would be announced. (3) The case on how to handle the prizes for the Shanghai Workers' Aircraft was resolved and handed over to the Shanghai Workers' Aircraft Committee.

The Fifth District Cigarette Industry Union held an emergency representative congress yesterday afternoon to discuss solutions to the difficult problem of wage reduction. More than 100 representatives attended the meeting. Zhou Lianze, a representative from the Municipal Party Headquarters, (vacancy), the Social Affairs Bureau, and Zheng Zhizhuang, a representative from the Municipal Public Security Bureau, attended the meeting for supervision. Matters resolved: (1) A resolution to issue a declaration in the name of the representative congress, stating responsibilities, was passed. (2) A resolution to send a letter in the name of the representative congress to the company's board of directors to increase working hours to maintain the livelihood of workers was passed. (3) A resolution that each representative should be nominated by the representative congress (limited to those who make cigarettes) to petition the party and government agencies, requesting increased work to maintain the lives of workers, was passed. (4) A resolution on whether workers in each factory would go to work tomorrow was resolved and the representatives would enter the factory, maintain order, and persuade them to wait for the party and government agencies to resolve the matter. Forecast of the Annual Meeting of the Economic Society

Discussing Economic Transformation Issues

A Total of Seven Days from August 21st

The annual meeting of the Chinese Economic Society was held in Hangzhou last August to discuss economic issues during the national crisis. A year has passed, and the annual meeting is being held in Qingdao starting on August 21st, and will last for a week until the 27th. The theme of the annual meeting's thesis is "Various Problems and Solutions Regarding China's Economic Transformation." The method for submitting papers has been notified to all members by the society's thesis committee. All those attending the meeting are requested to participate. Members who wish to submit papers can contact Mr. Li Zhaohuan of Jiaotong University at any time. The inspection locations are set as the rural construction in Jinan Zouping and the major cities along the Jiaoji Railway. In addition, we will visit Laoshan, Taishan, Qufu, and other places.

Minutes of the Annual Meeting of the Chinese Statistical Society

The Chinese Statistical Society is the only group in the statistical community in our country. The third annual meeting has already been held in Beijing. The meeting was held for several days. The situation is as follows: At 8 a.m. on the 13th, the opening ceremony was held at the Capital Academy of Political Accounting. About 100 people attended the meeting. Wang Zhongwu was elected as the chairman and delivered the opening speech. He said that the status of statistical science has been deeply recognized in today's Chinese society. Plans in all aspects of politics and economics are based on statistical figures as indicators. And the people who move this indicator are statisticians. Moreover, at a time when our country is in a national crisis, the preparation for wartime mobilization and the plan for maintaining the rural economy all require extremely numerical references. Therefore, the colleagues of this society should bear this heavy burden and serve the nation. There are three characteristics of this year's annual meeting that can be reported, namely (1) Strictly defining the qualifications of members, and members who join must have in-depth research and have made considerable contributions, (2) Focusing on academic research, the work of members is to study statistical science and clarify theories, without involving other affairs, (3) Fully preparing for the papers for this annual meeting. The papers read this time are all carefully crafted by the members, with unique insights, which can be used as a reference for the society. Then, Wang Luyi, a representative from the central government, delivered a speech, saying that the origin of statistics in our country is very ancient, but it has only recently become prosperous. This kind of work is even more necessary now. The Chinese Statistical Society is the crystallization of the statistical community in our country, and all the results of its research will definitely be the compass for all aspects of the country. Again, Minister of Education Wang Shijie delivered a speech, saying that there are many difficulties in the statistical undertaking in China. The first is that the general public does not understand the importance of statistics, and the second is the lack of talents engaged in this undertaking. If we want to make the statistical undertaking more and more glorious, we must break through the two difficulties. The scholars in the society are all well-known people, and I hope that they will work hard to move forward so that the statistical undertaking in China can shine in the world. Afterwards, representatives from the Municipal Party Headquarters and various agencies delivered speeches in succession. After that, the results of the election of the fourth session of the Society Affairs Committee were announced. Wang Zhongwu received 53 votes, Liu Dajun 51 votes, Wu Dajun 34 votes, Zhu Junyi 33 votes, Sun Zheng 30 votes, Sheng Jun 25 votes, Zhang Xinyi 23 votes, and Lin Wei 22 votes. They were elected as members of the Society Affairs Committee. After counting the votes, it was already 12 o'clock, and the Academy of Political Accounting feasted the members at the Central Hotel. In the afternoon, the reading of papers began. The papers included Zhu Zihui's "Comparison of Two Statistical Landscapes", Chu Yifei's "Matching Problems of Wave-type Curves" and "Algebraic Function Interpolation", Chen Huayin's "Trial Compilation of Economic Status Index", Zhu Junyi's "Statistical Research on the Years of Life of Famous People in China", Wu Dajun's "Environment and Thoughts of Chinese Youth" (a statistical observation), and other papers. The members also developed and discussed the topics, and the spirit was quite enthusiastic.

On the morning of the 14th, the reading of papers continued. The first was Wang Zhongwen's "Analysis of the Survey of Modern Chinese People", followed by Chen Zhengmo's "General Study on the Materials for Estimating the Population of Our Country", Chen Changheng's "Comparative Study of Population Statistics Since the Late Qing Dynasty", Chen Huayin's "Sex Ratio at Birth of Intellectual Class Population", Luo Zhiru's "Research on Simple Life Tables", Zhu Zihui's "Recent Wage Statistics of Chinese Official Offices", Wang Xichen's "Infant Mortality Rate in Nanjing", Liu Dajun's "New Method of Partial Correlation of Clothing Talent", Zheng Yanfen's "How to Estimate the Total Amount of Narcotics Needed in the World" and its Improper Consumption, etc., all of which were extremely valuable contributions. The meeting closed in the afternoon. At the same time, the fourth session of the Society Affairs Committee held a meeting, electing Wang Zhongwu as the president, Wu Dajun as the vice president, Zhu Junyi as the accountant, Sun Zheng as the document officer, and Sheng Jun, Zhang Xinyi, and Lin Wei as committee members. Liu Dajun was re-elected for three consecutive years. The meeting was adjourned after the election.

The International Trade Bureau Publishes the U.S. Prohibition on the Import of Rice Straw Packaging Regulations

The International Trade Bureau stated that the U.S. Consulate in Luo'anqi stated in a letter that from July 1 of this year, the import of various goods is prohibited from using plants or plant products as packaging materials. This has been reported in the previous newspaper. Now, the bureau, in order to draw the attention of Chinese merchants to the fact that many of our country's export goods use this material as packaging, has specially translated and published the full text of the announcement and the attached regulations as follows:

Announcement

The U.S. Packaging Material Quarantine Office, Announcement No. 69, stated that various plant products used as packaging materials, which are shipped from overseas, are prone to carrying germs, insects, or plant seedlings, which is related to the future of national agriculture and is very dangerous. Therefore, the import of plants has been banned in recent years. The import of dishes and vegetables must not be attached with green leaves. Eastern rice straw, used as packaging, has been found to carry germs in many surveys, and in large quantities. This germ is called (Rice Borer), which is a kind of plant parasite that is not easy to kill and is very harmful to plants. This germ is commonly found in rice-producing areas, but has not yet affected the American fields. In order to prevent malfeasance, all kinds of rice straw husks and chaff are prohibited from being imported. In addition to rice straw husks, etc., other items such as tree leaves, grass, mustard, and soil are also easy to carry plant germs, and they are also included in the ban. The use of these materials as packaging is far less common than rice straw, etc. Although the ban still has other items to replace, it will not affect commercial transportation in any way. In addition, items such as sugarcane, sorghum, cotton, and bamboo are subject to special regulations by the Quarantine Office and are also included in the ban. Regarding the above packaging materials, they must not be attached with plant germs. Inspectors have considerable authority to carry out all inspection procedures. Most ordinary items, such as various fillings, paper, wood chips, cork, firewood, and other kinds, are difficult to carry plant germs and are not within the scope of inspection.

Regulations

Article 1: From July 1, 1933, goods imported into the United States from all countries or regions must not use the following plants or plant products as packaging materials: (A) Rice straw, husks, and bran, etc. (all countries); (B) Millet (such as corn, sorghum, broomcorn, and other similar plants), except for imports from Mexico, Central America, South America, and the West Indies; other countries are not allowed to import them; (C) Cotton and cotton products (such as flax, waste cotton, cotton seeds, and cottonseed hulls, etc.) (all countries); (D) Sugarcane (including all parts of sugarcane and sugarcane dregs) (all countries); (E) Bamboo (including bamboo leaves and bamboo shoots) (all countries); (F) Plant leaves (all countries); (G) Tree bark (all countries); (H) Soil (containing a large amount of chlorophyll) (all countries).

Article 2: From July 1, 1933, goods imported into the United States from all countries or regions may use the following plants or plant products as packaging materials and in accordance with the regulations stipulated by the Quarantine Office: (1) Grain grasses, chaff, bran, and husks, excluding rice (such as wheat, buckwheat, barley, rye) (all countries); (2) Millet (such as corn, sorghum, broomcorn, etc.) (limited to those from Mexico, Central America, South America, and the West Indies); (3) Willow branches (limited to those from Europe); (4) Various dried fodders and herbaceous plants (all countries); (5) Soil (containing a large amount of plant matter, but only to the extent that it complies with the Quarantine Office's appendices and regulations).

Explanation

Article 1: Definitions. Section 1: The term "packaging material" in this chapter includes all the above-mentioned plants and plant products used in the shipment of goods as filling, binding, and for protection against moisture and breakage, etc. Section 2: Soil containing a significant amount of plant matter specifically refers to a type of soil containing decayed plant matter and carrying the risk of infectious bacteria. Pure mineral soil, etc., are not within the scope of quarantine. Section 3: Inspector. An inspector refers to an inspector from the United States Department of Agriculture.

Article 2: Exemption from germs. All imported packaging materials must not carry pests and plant pathogens.

Article 3: Import Inspection. All packaging materials imported must undergo inspection procedures.

Article 4: Handling of violations. For imported goods whose packaging materials violate the provisions of this regulation, and are confirmed by the inspector to carry infectious diseases or plant pathogens, the Quarantine Office may refuse the import of the goods, destroy the packaging materials, or perform other re-packaging and disinfection procedures.

Article 5: Regulations for soil used as filling material. The Quarantine Office stipulates that the following soil may be used as filling material: (1) Peat; (2) Peat moss; (3) Gsmuda Tidre.

Note: This regulation will take effect on July 1, 1933.

Father and Son Capture Rapist

Wang Fuju Molests Ms. Wang

In recent years, imported oiled paper has flooded the market, causing the decline of domestic oiled paper and severely impacting domestic manufacturers. The factory was named Tong Chang Domestic Improved Oiled Paper Factory. Sample papers were distributed to paper stores and users in various ports, all of whom were extremely satisfied. Its advantages are fourfold: (1) Oiled paper can generate heat when stored for a long time, and if not cared for regularly, it often self-ignites; (2) Ordinary oiled paper often becomes sticky between April and August due to the weather, causing it to clump together, but this improved domestic oiled paper has none of the above two problems; (3) The paper is strong and thick and does not stick to the touch; (4) The price is low. National Humiliation Week Lecture Mr. Chen Binhe Speaks on September 18th

Lecture at the YMCA on May 10 (continued)

A third thought: Before September 18th, it seemed that we had no national crisis! Everyone was living in a drunken dream, only caring about enjoying themselves. After September 18th, we suffered a de facto severe national crisis, losing one-thirteenth of our territory, one-twelfth of our population, and one-quarter of our property! Having suffered such a major national crisis, we should ask: What are the differences between the general situation before and after September 18th? Facts tell us that after September 18th, the Japanese government changed all factories in the country into factories manufacturing military supplies, and intensified the training of young people across the country, using various methods to incite the people to act against China. Everywhere shows a state of war. What about our government? After September 18th, a national crisis conference was held, many written protests were filed with the League of Nations, and many declarations were issued, advising the people to remain calm. Japanese scholars (not those hired by the government) advocated justice and opposed the government's policy of aggression. They advised the Japanese people not to blindly follow the government's policy of aggression. However, our scholars advocated peace talks, advocated acknowledging the facts, acknowledging the Twenty-One Demands, and advocated "we will wait another fifty years!" Let's see again, what did the Japanese bourgeoisie do after September 18th? They took out money to help the warlords invade China because they were of the same life. Our bourgeoisie still do their speculative business and live their lives of enjoyment! Let's see again, what about the Japanese working masses? Because Japanese imperialists want to expand their aggression and increase military spending, the working masses have not gained any benefits from the aggressive war but have increased their burden. The Chinese working masses, such as those in Zhabei and in the Northeast, directly suffered the ravages of imperialism. Or they indirectly suffered great pain, so the Chinese and Japanese working masses suffered equally after September 18th. Therefore, we know that only the Chinese and Japanese working masses can unite to smash Japanese imperialists and all traitors.

These thoughts are all unpleasant to hear. I now have another more pleasant thought, that is, after September 18th, the Northeast Volunteer Army and Ma Zhanshan, Su Bingwen, etc. rose up to resist, and the 19th Route Army rose up to resist on January 28th. This kind of struggle for self-defense to protect their own nation and country has been supported by the people of the whole country, sympathized with by the international community, and admired by the Japanese people!

We can now know that, from the perspective of a few thoughts, the only way we can go in the future is to fight for national survival! The history of the last few hundred years tells us that when the American Revolutionary War of 1778 failed, the French officer Lafayette said that the life of the American army was very hard, the soldiers were not full, and their clothes were not complete, and their skin was frozen black; but they all had a belief in demanding freedom and justice. They finally achieved victory through arduous and extraordinary efforts. When the Soviet Revolution took place, imperialist countries rose up to intervene by force. The Soviet Union had to resist as many as twelve fronts in the most difficult times, but it also achieved victory in the end. Turkey fought hard for three years in the war with Greece after the European War before declaring victory and becoming an independent country.

We now only have to fight for national survival. Only struggle is our way out, and only struggle can we survive!

After the September 18th Incident, Japan had two observations on China: The general warlords observed that the Chinese army was of no use in national defense, but was only a tool for the warlords to engage in political struggles in the country. They also said that the history of China is a history of being ruled by foreign nations in a cycle, a history of obeying all plans set by foreign nations. They also said that China is an unorganized country. Therefore, they despise China as not being their opponent! Another type of observation is from Japanese scholars. They believe that the September 18th Incident is of no benefit to Japan, but is like swallowing a bomb, but is sufficient to promote the unity of leaders from all parties in China, giving China an opportunity for unified cooperation, and giving China an opportunity for revitalization and innovation.

We don't know which of the two observations that the enemy made about us is correct!

The American War of Independence, the Soviet Revolutionary War, and the Turkish War of Resistance against Greece, we know from the facts in history! We know that the land we lost before can only be taken back by war in the future! We should understand that what we desire is the freedom and equality of China. This is a very valuable thing that cannot be obtained by paying a small price; we should prepare for the greatest sacrifice to repay this greatest price!

We still have to go through many setbacks, and we still have to go through many struggles before we can achieve national freedom and equality! (Recorded by Ye Wenxiong and Zhang Kuishi)

Free Talk

Two Types of People

— Bofu

In literature, there are two main types: prose and poetry. The same is true of people; there are two types: those with a prose temperament and those with a poet's temperament. A prose person is one who conforms himself to the world, while a poetic person is one who calls the world to conform to himself. For someone who conforms to the world, his ethics are extremely simple, namely, taking the good and bad of society as good and bad; his life is also extremely simple, namely, taking the life of society as his life; his purpose is even simpler, namely, taking what society calls success as success. Such a person has a simple purpose, a simple mind, and a simple spirit, but he is often the most successful person in society. As for someone with a poetic temperament, he wants the world to conform to himself, so he inevitably looks down on all life in the world, and thus is inevitably an idealist, a dreamer, and someone with a sensitive mind. His mind is complex, and his spirit is even more complex. He struggles throughout his life without knowing what his purpose is, and thus he only fails. Don't you often hear some county magistrates say, "We can't bear to take the money that others have the heart to take, so we're poor." That's right, this is what is called a poetic temperament.

A prose person outwardly flatters the poetic temperament, so he can get close to this kind of person to steal from him, rob him, and fool him. And he always flatters him highly on the altar of purity, lest he come down and cause trouble for his own career. China has been a land of humanity since ancient times, and scholars have always been held in high esteem, probably in this way.

A person with a poetic temperament looks down on this prose temperament, but he has no choice but to despise and scold him. As a result, the prose person takes advantage of what he disdains to do, does it himself, and thus succeeds in society.

The bad thing about a prose person is his dullness. As the saying goes, let him laugh and scold as he pleases, I will be a good official on my own. The bad thing about a poetic person is his vanity. He thinks he is not willing to be stained by the vulgar, so he becomes a straggler. He thinks he is pure, so he becomes a parasite.

Speaking of this, I am reminded of a story from my student days. When I was in Tokyo, my fellow villagers, classmates, those studying literature, and those studying martial arts were all at their peak. One day, we all gathered together for a chat. Among them, there was someone studying martial arts, whom we considered a straightforward and reckless man. He told us his future purpose with the unique dullness of a prose person. He said a lot frankly, which can be summarized as "getting promoted and getting rich."

Among us, there was also a gentleman studying literature, who probably couldn't bear to listen anymore, so he ridiculed him in a literary way, "Life is not just about getting promoted and getting rich!" What a poetic statement!

But do you know how that innocent and reckless man replied? He immediately replied, "You're right, naturally there's also marrying a wife, riding in a car, living in a Western-style house, etc. But if I get promoted and get rich, these things will naturally come."

He was not being humorous; he was just being frank. We laughed at him for being innocent, but in fact, we were all fooled by him. This is his secret to success.

Sure enough, I heard that he is now an official. And our gentleman studying literature is currently lacking food, even his wife looks down on him, and I heard that they are going to get divorced.

Digging Bunkers and Buying Airplanes

— Shiyi

Opening the newspaper, there are two lines of alarming headlines again: "Enemy forces are taking a surrounding shape on Pingjin, Japanese planes scout Peiping."

But looking closely, I realized that this news not only doesn't require us who read the newspaper on both sides to be alarmed, but even Peiping, where the planes are flying overhead, is "the officials are also very calm, and there is no sign of panic." This shows that although the troops of Japanese imperialism have been making steady progress on Chinese soil recently, the progress of the Chinese people's calmness skills is increasing day by day. According to the regulations by which a certain Central Committee member praised the calmness of Xuzhou students, an order should be given to commend them.

Unfortunately, the fly in the ointment is that the principals of the elementary schools in Peiping have gone to the Social Bureau to petition to "dig bunkers" in the schools, which is somewhat lacking in calmness; but it is not likely to alarm friendly nations to hide in bunkers to seek safety, and it may be appropriate to do so.

Digging a large bunker in every elementary school, moving the classrooms underground, and studying and reading with peace of mind regardless of the planes and bombs overhead, waiting quietly to study hard and save the country, to "recover lost territory," is truly a more tragic spectacle than Daudet's "The Last Lesson."

From the fact that elementary school students in Peiping are attending classes in bunkers, I am reminded of elementary school students in Shanghai raising donations in the streets. They forcibly drag people to throw some money into their bamboo tubes, saying that they will use it to buy airplanes to save the country.

If people bring airplanes, and we also bring airplanes to confront them, this is also a way to save the country.

But other people's airplanes have already flown over Peiping City, and our airplanes are still in the bamboo tubes of the elementary school students, how can it not make people sweat profusely with anxiety!

Someone said: You are wrong. Buying airplanes is not really going to fight against Japanese airplanes, but rather waiting until all of China's land is lost, and there is nowhere to place the Chinese nation, then like the "Noah's Ark" in the time of the Great Flood in ancient times, "sovereignty," "the people," etc. are all moved into the airplane to sail in the air. Therefore, it is called air rescue. If it is really for this purpose, we should indeed donate a few more dollars and buy a few more airplanes, lest there be nowhere to dig bunkers in the future.

Azalea

— Zhou Guangxi

Taking advantage of the blood-red azaleas, we went to Tianping Mountain for a day of fun.

I didn't have much lingering attachment to Tianping Mountain itself, but facing the azaleas on the way back, those azaleas that covered the hillside like shattered brocade under the setting sun in Shenxi, I felt a bit reluctant to leave.

I bent down and heartlessly picked a large handful of those tender azaleas, wanting to bring them back to Shanghai as a souvenir, but what good would that do? Once in Shanghai, these beautiful flowers would wither beyond recognition.

A melancholy mood, coupled with the desire to possess these flowers and leaves for a long time, made me even more cruel, digging up a budding plant with its roots. Although she clung tightly to the soil, she was finally carried on my cane all the way to Shanghai.

Upon returning to my Shanghai residence, I immediately planted her in a flowerpot, carefully placed in a cool spot on the balcony, watering her every day, hoping that this transplanted azalea could give me some comfort in this depressing city.

Unfortunately, the day after leaving Tianping Mountain, her flowers withered, and on the third and fourth days, her leaves withered. A week later, only a few dry and barren branches remained in the pot, ugly as the dry bones of the dead. Despite diligent watering, her life could not be saved. This suffocating city, this small flowerpot, was too unfamiliar to her, and she finally transformed into something lifeless.

Then I thought of the sedan chair carriers at the foot of Tianping Mountain, those sturdy, lively, honest, and simple women, each possessing a kind of vitality, a vitality of youthful life, which people in the city lack. But if these women were moved to the city, they would lose their strength, liveliness, honesty, and simplicity, and they would lose their youthful vitality. We only need to look at the female workers and maids from the countryside working in Shanghai factories and households to know this. Just like the azaleas on the mountain, which bloom with bright and beautiful flowers in nature, despite wind and rain, sun and dew, once moved to the city, they wither.

Because of the bankruptcy of the rural economy, because of the temptation of Shanghai's prosperity, every day, every hour, countless strong women are transported from the countryside, from the interior, to this city by trains and ships, to sacrifice their youth, their health and beauty, and even their lives!

Isn't this the same fate as the azaleas?

If people are like this, what does an azalea matter?

Looking at the withered azalea, my heart is filled with endless melancholy!

About Chinese Bees

— Li Xi

I once talked about the story of "robber bees," saying that Italian bees drove away Chinese bees. In fact, Chinese bees are always so unprogressive, and even without the introduction of Italian bees, there is always the possibility of extinction.

Chinese bees have too many enemies. The most harmful is the cotton worm, which often lives in the lower part of the beehive, gnawing through the beehive and stealing honey and pollen. They grow and develop, and when they occupy the honeycomb, the bees can do nothing but lead their colony to escape. Next is the honey moth, which is one or two inches long. When it invades, it also sucks honey and breaks the nest wax. The bees usually avoid it. Furthermore, swallows, sparrows, dragonflies, frogs, centipedes, snakes, and toads are all mortal enemies of bees. Among them, the toad is the most skillful and ruthless, opening its mouth and lazily waiting at the entrance of the beehive, waiting for the bees to crawl out of the hole, ready to work. It swallows them in one easy bite. A toad can eat more than fifty bees a day. Next is the "nine-mile bee". This kind of bee is more common near the mountains, smaller and fiercer than the honey moth. If one comes in, the only thing the beehive can do is escape quickly.

The things that Chinese bees fear, Italian bees don't take seriously at all. Italian bees have no other strengths, their only strength is working together to defend against enemies.

Chinese bees never have large colonies. As soon as they become slightly prosperous, they split again and again: one colony leaves today, another colony disappears tomorrow. Even the most experienced beekeepers can't guarantee when they will swarm. Small colonies, weak strength, and weak resistance also lead to poor work efficiency. When winter comes and food is scarce, they implement a suicidal policy: "gnawing wax." Chinese bees barely survive the winter, at least half of the worker bees die.

Recently, some people have started to improve them, believing that for Chinese bees to thrive and unite, unless each bee is coated with some sugar, perhaps they will see the sugar and suck each other, and will not leave for a while. Or sprinkle some glue on each bee's wings, so that they cannot be separated, in order to make them accustomed to group action.

However, this also requires foreigners to do it. In China, even people have always lacked things like sugar and glue.

Carrot Top

— Jules Renard, translated by Lin Quzuo

Arrangements (continued)

"When Mr. Lepic takes off his dirty leather shoes, I take them to the hallway, but Sister Ernestine would never let anyone else take the right to get slippers for Father. She embroidered flowers on these slippers herself.

"I take on some important errands that require long trips, such as to the pharmacist or doctor's house.

"You, on the other hand, are responsible for going to the village to buy small things.

"But regardless of whether it's sunny or raining, you have to go to the river to wash clothes for two or three hours every day. This is the most difficult task in your job, poor child; I can't help you with this at all. But if I have time, I can sometimes help you hang the clothes on the fence.

"I've thought of something: I'll give you a piece of advice. Don't dry the clothes on the fruit trees. Mr. Lepic won't blame you, but he will gently throw them on the ground, and when Mrs. Lepic finds a trace on the clothes, she will tell you to wash them again.

"Also, about the shoes, I have to give you a few words of advice. For the shoes you wear when hunting, you have to apply a lot of oil. Ordinary shoes only need a little polish.

"Don't clean those muddy pants too thoroughly. Mr. Lepic believes that pants covered in mud are more durable. He walks in those plowed fields and never ties up his trouser legs. When Mr. Lepic asks me to carry the game bag and follow him hunting, I would rather tie up my trouser legs.

"He said to me: 'Carrot Top, you will never become a true hunter.'

"And Mrs. Lepic said to me: 'Watch your ears, if you get yourself dirty.'

"It's a matter of taste for everyone.

"In short, you won't be too tired. When I'm home on vacation, you can share half of my work, and when my sister, brother, and I all go to school to stay, you can do less work. The result is the same.

"And no one will be too bad to you. If you ask the friends who come and go in our house, they will all guarantee you: my sister Ernestine is as gentle as an angel, my brother Felix has the best heart, Mr. Lepic has an upright spirit and sound judgment, and Mrs. Lepic has rare cooking skills. Perhaps I am the one in the family who you find the most difficult to deal with. Actually, I'm not like that. You just need to understand my personality. Besides, I am reasonable, I will change, and, without being immodest, I will make myself better, if you are a little humble, we can work together harmoniously.

"No, don't call me 'Sir'. Just call me Carrot Top like everyone else. It's shorter than 'Young Master Lepic'. But I ask you not to talk to me in that dismissive tone like your grandmother Olorin. Your grandmother's words often hurt me, I hate her very much."

Education News

Important News

Ministry of Education Orders Provincial Examinations in Lu Province to be Held in July

(Jinan, 16th) The Ministry of Education, considering that the provincial high school graduation examinations were originally scheduled for June 1st, fearing that students' studies would not be complete, postponed them to July. The Provincial Department of Education, fearing it would delay students' admission to higher education, requested that they be held on June 20th.

University Admissions Before the 24th Year Should Still Test on Party Principles

The Ministry of Education, in response to Shandong Tai University's inquiry as to whether university students should still be tested on Party principles during admission, and whether military academics are considered academic or technical subjects, specifically instructed the school to explain: "Your inquiry is noted. The examination subjects and levels of each subject for the admission of new students to schools above the vocational level should be handled in accordance with the newly promulgated high school curriculum standards from the 25th year onwards, as previously instructed by this Ministry's Order No. 10801. Before that year, schools should still conduct examinations on Party principles during the admission of new students. Furthermore, military academics refer to academic and technical subjects. You are hereby informed."

Ministry of Education Commends Individuals Who Donate Funds for Education

The Ministry of Education has issued certificates of commendation to individuals in various provinces and cities who donated funds for education in April. The names of the donors are as follows: (1) Two individuals were awarded first-class certificates: Zhu Zehuang from Changsha, Hunan, donated over 10,000 yuan to the Hunan Private Xiejun Junior High School Foundation. (2) Jiang Yuwen from Changde donated land and buildings worth over 42,300 yuan to the Jiang's Private Hanwen Junior High School in the 14th year of the Republic.

Standing Committee Meeting of the Chinese Education Society

丨Appointing Personnel for Educational Experiments and Socio-economic Survey Design丨

丨Compiling and Printing Two Special Publications: "Transformation of Chinese Education" and "Productive Education"丨

The second meeting of the Standing Committee of the Chinese Education Society was held the day before yesterday (the 13th) at the Jiangsu Provincial Educational College in Wuxi. Zheng Xiaocang, Xu Keshi, Chen Lijian, Chang Daozhi, Zheng Xigu, and others attended. Chairman: Zheng Xiaocang. The main agenda items are as follows: (1) How to regulate and raise funds for the Society: Resolution: Funds are divided into two categories: expenses for the Society and expenses for projects. The first category of expenses includes subsidies, printing, stationery, postage, annual meeting expenses, etc., which are paid from the Society's funds. The second category includes survey fees, experiment fees, and fees for purchasing a meeting place. In addition to donations from members of the Society, the remaining amount will be requested from administrative agencies for subsidies. (2) Please approve the first-term budget of the Society: Resolution: Passed as agreed. (3) Resolved to appoint Liu Naijing to be responsible for the design of the survey section, Xu Keshi to be responsible for the design of productive education experiments, Chen Lijian to be responsible for the design of civil education experiments, and Zheng Xigu to be responsible for the design of industrial education experiments. (4) Resolved to request local branches to earnestly assist in the implementation of local survey and experiment projects. (5) Resolved to send letters to the committees of each group, requesting them to actively carry out their work and report on their progress, submitting them no later than the end of June, and hoping to compile the results or materials obtained from the research into reports before the Double Tenth Festival for compilation and reporting. (6) How should non-periodic publications be handled this year? Resolution: First compile and print two special publications: "Transformation of Chinese Education" and "Productive Education". The deadline for collecting contributions is set for June 15th. (7) Resolved to add Meng Xiancheng and Chen Xuanzhen to assist in the editing of this year's special publication. (8) Resolved that local members' admission fees and annual membership fees should be collected and remitted by local fundraising committees, and sent to the general association no later than June 15th. (9) Resolved that the next plenary meeting of the Council will be held in Shanghai on June 30th.

University Association Cables Russian Ambassador Opposing Russian Sale of the Chinese Eastern Railway

▲According to the Agreement, the Railway is Jointly Owned by China and Russia

▲I Absolutely Cannot Recognize Unilateral Handling

The Shanghai University Student Union, in response to the Soviet Union's violation of the agreement and sale of the Chinese Eastern Railway, yesterday sent a special telegram to the Soviet Russian Ambassador to China, Bogomolov, in Nanjing, expressing opposition and requesting that the authorities of that country reconsider their attitude on this issue. The original telegram is summarized as follows: (Omitted address) "The issue of the sale of the Chinese Eastern Railway has been widely publicized internationally. According to a recent Reuters dispatch from Moscow, a conversation from Soviet Foreign Minister Litvinov stated that the sale of the Chinese Eastern Railway is an undeniable fact. Article 9, Section 5 of the 1924 Sino-Russian Agreement states that the sovereignty of the Chinese Eastern Railway belongs to the Republic of China and the Soviet Socialist Republic of the Soviet Union. The railway is jointly owned by China and Russia and cannot be disposed of without agreement. Now, in violation of the agreement and in disregard of good faith, the railway has been sold without authorization, intending to conclude an illegal act with an illegal organization. The Chinese people absolutely cannot recognize it and will seriously oppose it. We dare to request that your government pay attention to the agreement, reconsider its attitude on this issue, maintain sovereignty, and promote friendly relations. We are very eager to do so. Respectfully, the Shanghai University Student Union."
