Film Special

The Youth-Preserving Art of Female Stars

— Xing Zhi

Maintaining the Beauty of the Era of Twenty-Nine Years

Hollywood has this saying: "Movie actors have no age limit. From eighteen to eighty, anyone can be a star." But this statement is ultimately deceptive. Look at the many movie stars in Hollywood. Apart from Mary MacLaren, who is willing to play an aging old woman on the screen? Who doesn't want to play a charming young girl like a twenty-nine-year-old? Although very few are truly eighteen years old, several middle-aged women like Mary Pickford, Rose Talbot, Claire Windsor, Billie Burke, Marlene Dietrich, Lila Lee, and Gloria Swanson, if you don't know their age, who wouldn't say they are only seventeen or eighteen years old?

To gain a foothold in the film industry, they must of course maintain their youthful beauty. And maintaining youthful beauty has its secrets. This is not a temporary beauty treatment achieved by cosmetics, but a permanent way to prevent the skin from developing wrinkles and appearing old. Although this "permanent" can only last until around forty years old, it is still a major lesson in addition to the work of a movie actor. Mary Pickford's appearance can be said to be the most ageless among the stars. Her youth-returning technique is certainly very refined. She once said to people: "I believe that the word 'happiness' is the first element in avoiding aging. I often say that today's matters should be dealt with today, and I don't worry about yesterday's or tomorrow's matters. To put it bluntly, life is just this one thing. Only the present is precious, and there is no need to dwell on the past or worry about the future." This can be said to be Pickford's philosophy. Pickford is indeed the happiest person in Hollywood, and no one can make her angry. And after work, she always travels everywhere, leaving all worries behind. So her current charm is no less than when she was a teenager.

Rose Talbot said: "Aging" follows one's mood. One's mind should always be broader. I am not afraid of aging, but the more afraid, the easier it is to age. This must be known." Rose was a small star in 1909, but she is still very young.

Claire Windsor was called the most beautiful woman in Hollywood in 1920, and she is still as beautiful as she was thirteen years ago. According to her own words, she has never spent more than five minutes applying powder. She believes that powder is something that ruins people's appearance. There are also Lila Lee and Gloria Swanson, who are all skilled in this youth-preserving art.

Film Review

Review of Men Must Fight

— Zhou Yan

Distorted Consciousness, Excellent Techniques

In the extremely depressed current state of Hollywood, film companies are racking their brains to find a way out. This "Men Must Fight" was produced in this special situation. It takes the Second World War as its theme, although it is speculative, it is still imaginable that they admit to the inevitability of the Second World War. Of course, this drama will never advocate anti-imperialist aggressive war. On the contrary, it is the agitator of this cruel war. But is this the way out for American films? We can definitely say it is a "dead end." It escapes reality, grasps only dreams, and attempts to use narrow nationalistic concepts to mobilize people to participate in aggressive wars. The only excuse is that "peace cannot be spoken of without force." We believe that future wars can never be explained by national concepts, nor can they be eliminated by humanitarian pacifism. This film explains that Bob hates war because of Westworth, but later, after learning from his mother that his biological father was a martyr who died for his country, he flew a plane to participate in the war. This is obviously the most effective anesthetic.

In summary, the main significance of this film is entirely to flaunt the power of the American Air Force, preparing for and inciting the Second Massacre.

Although we say that it is distorted in consciousness, we cannot deny its success in technique. For example, the planes in the sky and the bombing of New York City are all very beautiful scenes. Although the destruction of huge buildings is fake, there is no trace of fabrication on the screen. Here we cannot help but admire their skillful use of light.

Of course, the best actor is Diana Wynyarde, who plays Laura, but in the end, I think she is too young, because after 1919 until 194, this long period of more than twenty years does not show any increase in age on her face.

Laura's ex-husband died in battle. When he was carried into the hospital, Laura discovered it before entering the door, and discovered that the deceased was her husband from the ornaments on his clothes. This subtle action is certainly the director's cleverness.

[Image description: Gu Meijun and Ms. Hu Ping, from the fashion show of the Chinese National Products Company on Nanjing Road before the war, resting together]

Audience Opinions

After Viewing "New Year's Eve"

— Yu Hong

The Consciousness is Narrow and Not of the Masses

The plot of this film revolves around the essence of joy, anger, sorrow, and happiness that unfolds during the twelve hours of New Year's Eve. This is indeed novel. However, because the time frame is so short, the director cannot provide detailed portrayals of the characters' backgrounds and personalities. Therefore, the audience only receives a partial impression, lacking a complete emotional experience. In this regard, it falls short of "Morning of the City" and "Night of the City."

Regarding the consciousness conveyed, we dare not say it is sound. In the current era, films with socialist themes should seek natural development through the "determination" of individuals or groups, not rely on traditional ideas of "old morality" and "old etiquette" to solve everything. The film ends with a wealthy banker generously donating money to pay off the debts of the old scholar Liu. However, can every poor person encounter such a generous person? And does such generosity even exist in modern society? Regarding these two points, we can see that the consciousness of "New Year's Eve" is narrow and not of the masses.

After Watching "New Year's Eve"

— Feng Ying

The Director's Skills Are Still Quite Exquisite

The long-awaited "New Year's Eve" has finally been released to the public in Beijing. When the reporter arrived at 5 o'clock, the seats were already almost full. From this, we can see that the audience has a considerable affection for domestic films.

The story of the film is very simple, only depicting several different comedies of sorrow, joy, separation, and reunion in just a few hours of a day.

The debt collector in the plot tells us that one should be subservient to the rich but fierce and intimidating to the poor. As for the scene where the debt collector, having lost the money, attempts to drown himself, it is illogical for him to suddenly say, "We should strive to break this terrible environment" after encountering the old man. How could he understand the need for active struggle yet attempt suicide over three hundred yuan?

The meaning is mediocre, but the director's skills are still quite exquisite, and the pacing is tight.

As for the actors, Liu Jiqun, in such a heroic role, shows us the Oriental Harold Lloyd. This change in style undoubtedly shows significant progress. Chen Yanyan, in "Spring in the South" and "Struggle," has already given us a deep impression. This time, she can even better display her artistic talent. Jiang Junchao's expressions are very realistic, and the rest are commendable.

My View of "New Year's Eve"

— Chen Benrong

Pointing Out Several Far-Fetched Aspects

The title is very beautiful, but the script's fantasy and the structure's forced nature are regrettable. Fortunately, the director worked hard, and it is still a good work. In addition to the plot already reviewed, there are still several inconsistencies, as follows:

1. The dance hall manager gives Third Sister 300 yuan to buy a dancer, but Third Sister – a cunning woman – doesn't deduct any commission when giving it to the old man's wife. And the old man's wife – who had taken the money the old man pawned to repay gambling debts – also gives the full amount to the old man. Isn't this a bit contradictory?

2. The old man's daughter becomes a dancer, both willingly and then runs back home.

3. The aspiring young volunteer wants to commit suicide over 300 yuan, and tells the old man, "We must strive to overcome all difficulties," but then innocently accepts the old man's money without refusing, and the amount is conveniently just right.

4. Teaching someone to dance in a few hours and then having them perform on stage is too fast.

5. The dance hall's business is very good, so its income must be good; how could it be in debt to the money lender?

As for the director, he is indeed very dedicated. He does not use subtitles to resolve the difficulties in the visuals. In terms of technique: such as the close-up when the old man returns the money to the rich lady, and the teacup in the old man's home having no tea, these are good. The leads, Chen Yanyan and Liu Jiqun, are the best, and the supporting actress Xing Shaomei is better. This film is entirely night scenes, but the kitchen in the old man's house is too bright. The snow on the ground looks real, but the falling snow is all paper, etc. These small mistakes should be avoided in future productions.

After Watching "New Year's Eve"

— Yu Jiaqing

Made Me Discover a New Star

"New Year's Eve" depicts the "hardships" and "difficulties" of poor people passing the New Year. The general story is about an old man who is pressured by many debt collectors on New Year's Eve, and his wife sells their daughter to a dance hall to be a dancer. Unexpectedly, the dance hall manager abuses and bullies her. She is desperate and still runs back home. Later, the old man helps a young man in need, and in the end, the young man and the money lender help the old man out of his predicament.

Actors such as Liu Jiqun have completely changed their style, with no trace of comedic elements. Chen Yanyan's performance shows significant progress compared to her previous roles. Jiang Junchao gives the most successful performance in this film. I say he is about to occupy an important position in the film industry, and will be a new star of 1933. The other actors do not have any special performances.

The Movie Novel "The White Sister" (Part One)

— Si Ping

Produced by MGM, Starring Helen Hayes

Sacrificing Reputation and Happiness for Love

Inside the church, Angela sits between her father and her fiancé, attending mass. She feels that her life is as fulfilling and beautiful as the rose window of the chapel, charming, and with a touch of emptiness. At the end of the service, Pastor Sala Sinnaser announces from the pulpit for the third time the good news of the upcoming marriage of Ennas Duto and Angela, the beloved daughter of Quito Shermont.

Her father's hand gently takes Angela's jade arm, giving a gesture of affection. She repays him with a sweet smile. She does not feel a sting in her heart for this formal announcement that is enough to move her. She has accepted her father's marriage arrangement for her as she unquestioningly and unremarkably obeys the other plans her father makes for her. Prince Shermont listens to this report and sincerely thanks God for the success of the good deed.

As the piano plays the closing hymn of the service, they rise and walk out of the dimness of the church into the bright sunlight on the stone steps. The scenery here is beautiful, a world apart from the state of mind when attending mass. A carnival is being held in the square, with dazzling sights and sounds, the waves of laughter echoing the piano music coming from the church.

Relatives and friends gather around, vying to congratulate the engaged couple, but Angela looks distracted at the lively carnival, feeling endless interest. As her father helps her into the car, she repeatedly looks back, expressing her reluctance to leave the carnival. As the car starts, she says eagerly:

"Should we take that road? We can watch the dancing – don't you like to watch dancing, Ennas Duto?"

"Not very much." Ennas Duto smiles at her, and her father shakes his head, as if the request is unworthy of attention.

"Look at their faces, Father! They're so interesting," Angela says, gazing out the car window as it passes by. "Every day should be a carnival day! There should always be music! And dancing!"

Seeing that her father and fiancé are not listening to her, her enthusiasm fades away. They casually chat, getting along well. However, Angela leans over, sticks her head out of the window, and throws her purse to a beggar on the side of the road. The old woman thanks her repeatedly, and Angela smiles sweetly, their conversation interrupted by this incident.

"I'm sorry, Ennas Duto," she says quickly, apologizing when she sees a look of displeasure on his face. "I'm sorry, Father." She sits back, her slender arms crossed over her chest, as if to hold the fleeting pleasure tightly in her heart.
